width="31" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ellipse_sign_127.svg/47px-Ellipse_sign_127.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ellipse_sign_128.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_128.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.yaucoatuservicio.com">www<wbr />.yaucoatuservicio<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Yauco</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xcb\x88\xca\x9dawko&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Yauco_barrio-pueblo" title="Yauco barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in southern <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Although the <a href="/wiki/Yauco_barrio-pueblo" title="Yauco barrio-pueblo">downtown</a> is inland, the municipality stretches to a southern coast facing the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. Yauco is located south of <a href="/wiki/Maricao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maricao, Puerto Rico">Maricao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lares,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lares, Puerto Rico">Lares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adjuntas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Adjuntas, Puerto Rico">Adjuntas</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Grande, Puerto Rico">Sabana Grande</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica, Puerto Rico">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Guayanilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guayanilla, Puerto Rico">Guayanilla</a>. The municipality consists of 20 barrios and <a href="/wiki/Yauco_barrio-pueblo" title="Yauco barrio-pueblo">Yauco Pueblo</a> (the downtown and administrative center of the municipality). It is both a principal town of the <a href="/wiki/Yauco_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Yauco Metropolitan Statistical Area">Yauco Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ponce-Yauco-Coamo,_PR_CSA" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce-Yauco-Coamo, PR CSA">Ponce-Yauco-Coamo Combined Statistical Area</a>.\n</p><p>It was founded by Fernando Pacheco on February 29, 1756, and developed for commodity crops of <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugar cane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production" title="Coffee production">coffee</a>. Yauco became a center for <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico</a> in the 19th century due to its geographical similarity to their homeland. <a href="/wiki/Corsicans" title="Corsicans">Corsicans</a> have contributed to many areas of life in Yauco, particularly to its <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Coffee production in Puerto Rico">coffee industry</a>. This has played a role in the town\'s nicknames of <i>El Pueblo del Caf\xc3\xa9</i> (Town of Coffee), and residents of the municipality are often referred to as <i>Los Corsos</i> (The Corsicans).\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><b>Yauco</b> was named after the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Yauco" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Yauco">Yauco River</a>, which itself comes from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word <i><span title="Taino-language text"><i lang="tnq">coayuco</i></span></i>, meaning "<a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> plantation" (also where the word <i>yucca</i> comes from).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city has numerous nicknames such as <i>Pueblo del Caf\xc3\xa9</i> ("coffee town"), due to the high number of coffee plantations in the area, and <i>Pueblo de los Corsos</i> ("Town of <a href="/wiki/Corsicans" title="Corsicans">Corsicans</a>"), after the large number of <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsican immigrants</a> who settled in the town and who were later influential to the area\'s coffee industry. It is also popularly known as <i>La Capital Ta\xc3\xadna</i> ("the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> capital") after the native peoples of Puerto Rico who also lived in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Taino</a> natives considered the area of Yauco the capital of <i>Boriken</i> and was governed by <a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%BCeyban%C3%A1_(The_Great_Sun)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 (The Great Sun)">Ag\xc3\xbceybana</a>, the most powerful Ta\xc3\xadno <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a></i> (chief) in the island. All the other caciques were subject to and had to obey Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1, although they governed their own tribes. Upon Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1\'s death in 1510, his nephew, G\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 (also known as <a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%BCeyban%C3%A1_II" title="Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 II">Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 II</a>), became the most powerful cacique in the island. Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 II doubted the "godly" status the Spaniards were rumored to have. He came up with a plan to test these doubts: he and <a href="/wiki/Urayo%C3%A1n" title="Urayo\xc3\xa1n">Urayo\xc3\xa1n</a> (cacique of <a href="/wiki/A%C3%B1asco,_Puerto_Rico" title="A\xc3\xb1asco, Puerto Rico">A\xc3\xb1asco</a>) sent some of their tribe members to lure a Spaniard named <a href="/wiki/Diego_Salcedo_(soldier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Diego Salcedo (soldier)">Diego Salcedo</a> into a river and drown him. They watched over Salcedo\'s body to ensure that he did not revive. Salcedo\'s death convinced Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 II and the rest of the Ta\xc3\xadno that the Spaniards were not gods. They rebelled against the Spanish in 1511 but were defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-Rebellion_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebellion-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cacique_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cacique-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1755, the <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> settlers of the region built a small chapel and named it <i>Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Sant\xc3\xadsimo Rosario</i> (Our Lady of the Holy Rosary). The settlers sent Fernando Pacheco as their representative to the Spanish Government, to request the establishment of a municipality, since they had satisfied one of the requirements for the establishment of a municipality, namely, to establish a place of worship. On February 29, 1756, the King of Spain granted the settlers their request and the town of Yauco was founded. Fernando Pacheco was named First Lieutenant of War of the new town.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>From the mid-19th to the early 20th century, hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="French immigration to Puerto Rico">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Irish immigration to Puerto Rico">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="German immigration to Puerto Rico">German</a> immigrants arrived in Puerto Rico, attracted by the Spanish Crown\'s offer of free land to Catholic white European settlers. They settled mostly in the south-central region.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="19th_century_Corsican_immigration">19th century Corsican immigration</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th century Corsican immigration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico</a></div><p>\nThe island of Puerto Rico is somewhat similar in geography to the island of <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and appealed to many <a href="/wiki/Corsicans" title="Corsicans">Corsican</a> immigrants. Corsica was part of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> for centuries until 1768.</p><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_Corsican_Plaque.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Historical_Corsican_Plaque.jpg/220px-Historical_Corsican_Plaque.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/12/Historical_Corsican_Plaque.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="287" data-file-height="267" /></a><figcaption>Memorial dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsicans</a> in Yauco.</figcaption></figure><p>Corsicans descend from a combination of ancient <i>Corsi</i> people from northeastern <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> and people who came over later from northern and <a href="/wiki/Central_Italy" title="Central Italy">central Italy</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ligures" title="Ligures">Ligurians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>) along with, to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punic_people" title="Punic people">Carthaginians</a>. Corsica has been part of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> since 1768 but retains a distinct <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Italy" title="Culture of Italy">Italian culture</a>. It was ruled by the Republic of Genoa from 1284 to 1755, when it became a self-proclaimed independent <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>-speaking Republic. In 1768, Genoa officially ceded its out of control colony to <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV" title="Louis XV">Louis XV</a> of France as part of a pledge for debts, and in 1769 France forcibly annexed it.\n</p><p>Hundreds of Corsicans and their families immigrated to Puerto Rico from as early as 1830, and their numbers peaked in the 1850s, after European unrest following the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, and environmental problems of lengthy drought. The Corsicans tended to settle in the mountainous southwestern region of the island, and Yauco attracted the majority of them.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As noted, the three main crops were coffee, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> and tobacco. The new settlers first worked on the farms, and some saved money in order to own and operate their own grocery stores. They began to specialize in cultivation of coffee as a commodity crop.\n</p>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yauco_Coffee_Plantation.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Yauco_Coffee_Plantation.gif/250px-Yauco_Coffee_Plantation.gif" decoding="async" width="250" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Yauco_Coffee_Plantation.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="312" data-file-height="200" /></a><figcaption>Early Yauco coffee plantation (Pre-1920)</figcaption></figure><p>Coffee was first cultivated in the Rancheras and Diego Hern\xc3\xa1ndez sectors; it was expanded to the <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Blancas,_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Blancas, Yauco, Puerto Rico">Aguas Blancas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frailes,_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico" title="Frailes, Yauco, Puerto Rico">Frailes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rubias,_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rubias, Yauco, Puerto Rico">Rubias</a> sectors. The Mariani family adapted a <a href="/wiki/Cotton_gin" title="Cotton gin">cotton gin</a> in the 1860s to use in mechanical <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production" title="Coffee production">de-husking of coffee</a>. This improved the appearance of Puerto Rico\'s coffee beans and helped it stand out in the international coffee market.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the 1860s the Corsican settlers were the leaders of the coffee industry in Puerto Rico, and seven out of ten coffee plantations were owned by Corsicans.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Intentona_de_Yauco">Intentona de Yauco</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Intentona de Yauco"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Intentona_de_Yauco" title="Intentona de Yauco">Intentona de Yauco</a></div><figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg/200px-Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg/300px-Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg/400px-Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="363" /></a><figcaption>Flag flown by Fidel V\xc3\xa9lez and his men during the "Intentona de Yauco" revolt</figcaption></figure><p>The pro-independence movement raised the second and last major revolt here against <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colonial rule</a> in Puerto Rico, known as the <a href="/wiki/Intentona_de_Yauco" title="Intentona de Yauco">Intentona de Yauco</a> (the <i>attempted Coup of Yauco</i>). The revolt, which occurred on March 26, 1897, was organized by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Mattei_Lluberas" title="Antonio Mattei Lluberas">Antonio Mattei Lluberas</a>, Mateo Mercado and Fidel V\xc3\xa9lez. They were supported by leaders of <a href="/wiki/El_Grito_de_Lares" class="mw-redirect" title="El Grito de Lares">El Grito de Lares</a>, the first major independence attempt, who were in exile in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> as members of the Puerto Rican Revolutionary Committee. During this uprising, V\xc3\xa9lez raised for the first time what became the current <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Flag of Puerto Rico">flag of Puerto Rico</a> on local soil. Local Spanish authorities had heard rumors of the revolt and acted swiftly to suppress it.<sup id="cite_ref-HMPR_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HMPR-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American_War"><span id="Spanish.E2.80.93American_War"></span>Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_(page_222_crop).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg/100px-Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="195" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg/150px-Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg/200px-Cr%C3%B3nica_de_la_guerra_hispano-americana_en_Puerto_Rico_%28page_222_crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="641" data-file-height="1251" /></a><figcaption>Juan Mar\xc3\xada Morciglio was one of the men who stayed.</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Campaign">Puerto Rico Campaign</a></div><p>In 1898, upon the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica" class="mw-redirect" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a> was a small <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrio</a> within the municipality of Yauco. It had 60 houses in all and was defended only by eleven members of the 4th Volante de Yauco, a Puerto Rican militia unit, under the command of Lieutenant Enrique M\xc3\xa9ndez L\xc3\xb3pez. When the convoy with General <a href="/wiki/Nelson_A._Miles" title="Nelson A. Miles">Nelson A. Miles</a>, approached the barrio, <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica_Light" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica Light">Gu\xc3\xa1nica lighthouse</a> keeper Robustiano Rivera immediately alerted its residents. Nearly all the residents abandoned their homes and joined Rivera to go to Yauco, where he broke the news of the invading forces to the town\'s mayor. Only Agust\xc3\xadn Barrenechea, Vicente Ferrer, Juan Mar\xc3\xada Morciglio, Sim\xc3\xb3n Mejil, Salvador Mu\xc3\xb1oz, Cornelio Serrano and Pascual Elena stayed to welcome the invaders.<sup id="cite_ref-EDG_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDG-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> </p><figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg/250px-Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg/375px-Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/Yauco_Battlefield_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="288" /></a><figcaption>Part of the Hacienda Desideria, owned by Antonio Mariani, where the Battle of Yauco took place in 1898</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The first skirmish between Spanish/Puerto Rican and American armed forces was fought in that barrio between the Puerto Rican militia and twenty-eight sailors and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marines</a>, under the command of Lieutenants H. P. Huse and Wood. They had come from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Gloucester_(1891)" title="USS Gloucester (1891)">USS&#160;<i>Gloucester</i></a> on rafts and landed on the beach, where Lt. M\xc3\xa9ndez L\xc3\xb3pez and his men opened fire on the Americans. During the small battle which followed, the Americans returned fire with a machine gun and the <i>Gloucester</i> began to bombard the Spanish position. Lt. M\xc3\xa9ndez L\xc3\xb3pez and three of his men were wounded, and the militia unit retreated to the town of Yauco.\n</p><p>This was also the site of the first major land battle in Puerto Rico during the war between Spanish/Puerto Rican and American armed forces. On July 26, 1898, Spanish forces and Puerto Rican volunteers, led by Captain Salvador Meca and Lieutenant Colonel Francisco Puig, fought against American forces led by Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/George_A._Garretson" title="George A. Garretson">George A. Garretson</a>. The Spanish forces engaged the 6th Massachusetts in a firefight at the Hacienda Desideria, owned by Antonio Mariani, in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Desideria" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Desideria">Battle of Yauco</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Campaign">Puerto Rico Campaign</a>. The casualties of Puig\'s forces were two officers and three soldiers wounded and two soldiers dead. The Spanish forces were ordered to retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-BY_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BY-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Significant rainfall from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in Yauco, leaving entire communities cut-off.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Yauco_River" title="Yauco River">Yauco River</a> caused flooding that decimated entire neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-END_Yauco_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-END_Yauco-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Earthquakes_in_2019_and_2020">Earthquakes in 2019 and 2020</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Earthquakes in 2019 and 2020"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Puerto_Rico_earthquakes" title="2019\xe2\x80\x9320 Puerto Rico earthquakes">2019\xe2\x80\x9320 Puerto Rico earthquakes</a></div>\n<p>Multiple residences and structures in Yauco were damaged in a <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Puerto_Rico_earthquakes" title="2019\xe2\x80\x9320 Puerto Rico earthquakes">series of earthquakes with increasing magnitude</a> that started on December 28, 2019 and culminating with a 6.4-magnitude earthquake that struck the island in the morning hours of January 7, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> More than thirty-two residences collapsed and hundreds were structurally unsound after the earthquake struck near Yauco. To aid residents who were left without power or homeless, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico National Guard">National Guard</a> was mobilized. A center for emergency operations was set up in the municipality\'s auditorium parking area, with air-conditioned tarps and tents for evacuated hospital patients and with food being cooked by <a href="/wiki/World_Central_Kitchen" title="World Central Kitchen">World Central Kitchen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Yauco is a mountainous municipality located in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> and bisected by the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Yauco" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Yauco">R\xc3\xado Yauco</a>. Other rivers in the municipality are the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Chiquito_(Yauco,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Chiquito (Yauco, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Chiquito</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Duey_(Yauco,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Duey (Yauco, Puerto Rico)">Duey Loco</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Naranjo_(Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado Naranjo (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Naranjo</a>. Hills in the area include Mount Membrillo, the highest point in the municipality and 9th highest peak in the island at 3,579 feet (1,090 m) of elevation,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Pico_Rodadero" title="Pico Rodadero">Rodadero Peak</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Curet Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrios_of_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img /></a><figcaption>Pueblo of Yauco</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Yauco is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style Rico">Vegas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yauco_barrio-pueblo" title="Yauco barrio-pueblo">Yauco barrio-pueblo</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Yauco: Diego Hern\xc3\xa1ndez, Frailes, Ranchera, Sector Primitivo Irizarry in Quebradas, El Pozo, Sector Cantera, Pueblo Norte (El Cerro), and R\xc3\xado Prieto.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> the population of Yauco in the year 2000 was 46,384 persons, decreasing to 42,043 persons in <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010</a>, a net loss of 4,341 people or 9.36% of its population. The urban zone accounted for 17,186 of its inhabitants in the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The 2020 census indicated the population was 34,172 a decline of 18.7% from the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yaucromatic.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Yaucromatic.jpg/220px-Yaucromatic.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Yaucromatic.jpg/330px-Yaucromatic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Yaucromatic.jpg/440px-Yaucromatic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="4608" /></a><figcaption>"Yaucomatric" in <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cerro de Yauco</i></span> in Yauco barrio-pueblo</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Casa_Agostini_-_Yauco_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3640" data-file-height="2754" /></a><figcaption>Casa Agostini in Yauco</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Following <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, in order to lift up their spirits, Yauco\'s artists worked on "Yaucromatic", a project to paint colorful murals in <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cerro de Yauco</i></span> in Yauco barrio-pueblo.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are 2 beaches in Yauco, including <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Playa Ballenas</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nSome of the places of interest in Yauco include:\n</p><p><b>At <a href="/wiki/Yauco_barrio-pueblo" title="Yauco barrio-pueblo">Yauco Pueblo</a> (the historic downtown):</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Casona_C%C3%A9sari" title="Casona C\xc3\xa9sari">Cesari House</a>, historic house from 1893.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chalet_Amill" title="Chalet Amill">Chalet Amill</a>, Beax Arts-style house from 1914.</li>\n<li>Cuesta Los Judios (Spanish for "ascent of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Puerto_Rico" title="History of the Jews in Puerto Rico">Jews</a>"), next to <i>Reparto La Esperanza</i> it has a length of 0.21 kilometres.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Filardi_House" title="Filardi House">Filardi House</a>, Beaux Arts-style house from 1916.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Franceschi_Antongiorgi" title="Casa Franceschi Antongiorgi">Franceschi Antongiorgi House</a>, Beaux Arts-style house from 1907.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Residencia_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Vivaldi" title="Residencia Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Vivaldi">Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Vivaldi House</a>, Criollo-style house from 1880.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Logia_Mas%C3%B3nica_Hijos_de_la_Luz" title="Logia Mas\xc3\xb3nica Hijos de la Luz">Logia Mas\xc3\xb3nica Hijos de la Luz</a>, the historic masonic lodge from 1894.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Agostini" title="Casa Agostini">Negroni Mansion</a>, also known as the Agostini House, a Classical Revival-style house designed by Miguel Briganti Pinti.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Church_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_del_Rosario_of_Yauco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Church Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Rosario of Yauco (page does not exist)">Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Rosario Church</a> and City Hall at <i>Plaza Fernando Pacheco.</i></li>\n<li>Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Rosario Hermitage Ruins, just outside the city center, today a museum and ruins.</li>\n<li>Sant\xc3\xadsimo Rosario School, a school located in a historic building.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Teatro_Ideal" title="Teatro Ideal">Teatro Ideal</a>, a historic theater which was inaugurated on April 24, 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS_2021_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS_2021-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Yaucromatic</i> painted houses and murals.</li></ul>\n<p><b>Elsewhere in Yauco:</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Apiturismo honey production farm dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Agritourism" title="Agritourism">agritourism</a>.</li>\n<li>Atolladora Beach, shared with Guayanilla.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guilarte_State_Forest" title="Guilarte State Forest">Guilarte State Forest</a>, shared with Adjuntas, Guayanilla and Pe\xc3\xb1uelas.</li>\n<li>Hacienda Mireia, also known as Hacienda La Juanita, a historic plantation, is a 50-acre coffee farm.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lake_Luchetti" title="Lake Luchetti">Lake Luchetti</a>, a reservoir and wildlife refuge named after engineer <a href="/wiki/Antonio_S._Luchetti" title="Antonio S. Luchetti">Antonio S. Luchetti</a>.</li>\n<li>Mario "\xc3\x91ato" Ram\xc3\xadrez Torres Municipal Stadium</li>\n<li>Mount Membrillo, the highest mountain in the municipality and 9th tallest in Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pico_Rodadero" title="Pico Rodadero">Pico Rodadero</a>, the second highest mountain in the municipality.</li>\n<li>Ra\xc3\xbal "Pipote" Oliveras Vera Coliseum</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sus%C3%BAa_State_Forest" title="Sus\xc3\xbaa State Forest">Sus\xc3\xbaa State Forest</a>, shared with <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Grande, Puerto Rico">Sabana Grande</a>.</li>\n<li>Tozza Castle, replica of a small castle in Corsica, built by the Gilormini family.</li>\n<li>Volkyland Museum, dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Beetle" title="Volkswagen Beetle">Beetle</a> or Bug.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Yauco page lists the murals at Yaucromatic, the view from the top of a mountain in Sierra Alta called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Pico Rodadero</i></span>, the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Refugio de Vida Silvestre del Embalse Luccieti</i></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and (for <a href="/wiki/Agritourism" title="Agritourism">agritourism</a>) a honey production farm in <span title="Spanish-language text"><span lang="es" style="font-style: normal;">barrio Diego Hernandez</span></span> called Apiturismo,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Yauco\'s main crops are coffee, plantains, oranges and tobacco. Yauco coffees are a revived specialty origin that, at best, display the qualities that made <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Blue_Mountain_Coffee" title="Jamaican Blue Mountain Coffee">Jamaica Blue Mountain</a> famous: A deep, vibrant, yet restrained acidity and balanced, gently rich flavor. However, this potentially finest of Caribbean coffees is often marred by inconsistency.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Coffee production and sales from Yauco reached faraway places such as Europe in the 19th century and many non-Yauco coffee producers even tried to link their products to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cafe_Yaucono&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cafe Yaucono (page does not exist)">Cafe Yaucono</a> is a well-known Puerto Rican coffee brand that is named after Yauco.\n</p><p>Yauco also produces textiles and other light manufactured materials.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sartorius_AG" title="Sartorius AG">Sartorius</a> pharmaceuticals, located in Yauco, expanded their current operations there in mid 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Yauco celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in October. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de Nuestra Virgen del Rosario</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Yauco include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Coffee Festival \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> Festival - December</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival Internacional de las Culturas</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 December<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="DNA_Ancestry_Tests">DNA Ancestry Tests</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: DNA Ancestry Tests"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Recent genealogical DNA-based testing, which look at specific locations of a person\'s genome, in order to find or verify ancestral genealogical relationships or to estimate the ethnic mixture of an individual, have found significant <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsicans" title="Corsicans">Corsican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> European, <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North African</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Europe" title="History of the Jews in Europe">European Jewish</a> DNA presence in individuals who are descendants from inhabitants who were born within the geographical area of Yauco and other parts of southwestern Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>These ethnicities have significantly influenced the local culture, to include food, art, some words used in the language, customs, beliefs, and music.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>In 2019, Angel Luis Torres is the mayor of Yauco.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Abel_Nazario_Qui%C3%B1ones" class="mw-redirect" title="Abel Nazario Qui\xc3\xb1ones">Abel Nazario Qui\xc3\xb1ones</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="New Progressive Party of Puerto Rico">New Progressive Party</a> had held the office of Mayor of Yauco since 2000. He succeeded Pedro Jaime Torres by winning the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2000">2000 general election</a> and retained his seat in both <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2004">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_General_Elections_of_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico General Elections of 2008">2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nazario took a 50% pay cut which was reversed in 2005, yet his current annual wage of $36,000 is the lowest for any of the 78 Puerto Rican mayors, despite Yauco not being the least-populated municipality or the one with the lowest budget.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Yauco belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district V">Puerto Rico Senatorial district V</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Ruiz" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz">Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Vargas_Morales" title="Mart\xc3\xadn Vargas Morales">Mart\xc3\xadn Vargas Morales</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a>, were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg/220px-USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg/330px-USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg/440px-USDOT_FHWA_NHS_Yauco%2C_Puerto_Rico_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a><figcaption>"Interstate" Highway PRI-2 goes through Yauco. Urbanized areas are shaded in peach.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Roads_in_Puerto_Rico#Interstate_Highway_System" title="Roads in Puerto Rico">Interstate Highway</a> <a href="/wiki/PRI-2" class="mw-redirect" title="PRI-2">PRI-2</a> goes through Yauco. The <i>interstate</i> highway is designated as such because it receives up to 90% of its funding from the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">US Interstate Highway System</a>.\n</p><p>In 2019, there were 40 bridges in Yauco.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A bridge that goes over <a href="/wiki/Yauco_River" title="Yauco River">Yauco River</a> suffered damages during 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-END_Yauco_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-END_Yauco-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A bridge that carries PR-359 would have to be demolished due to damages caused by the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Puerto_Rico_earthquakes" class="mw-redirect" title="2019\xe2\x80\x932020 Puerto Rico earthquakes">2019\xe2\x80\x932020 Puerto Rico earthquakes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag of Yauco consists of two horizontal stripes of equal width, black the superior and gold the inferior one. The municipal coat of arms is in the center.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The coat of arms of Yauco is quartered by a central cross representing <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>.\nIn a silver field a gold and black boiler, with seven necks and heads of black serpents in each handle, three to the right hand, confronted with four to the left-hand side. Bordered by a checkered band in gold and black. The second and third quarters, in a field of gold, two coffee plant flowers of five leaves of silver and four red. The <a href="/wiki/Coffea" title="Coffea">coffee plant</a> flower and the coffee grains represent their cultivation in the Yauco municipality. The border of the Arms represents the beads of the rosary. The four-tower crown represents its town status.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yauco,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable people"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main category: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Yauco,_Puerto_Rico" title="Category:People from Yauco, Puerto Rico">People from Yauco, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>The following is a list of people born in Yauco.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Elmer_Rom%C3%A1n" title="Elmer Rom\xc3\xa1n">Elmer Rom\xc3\xa1n</a> (born 1972) -  26th Secretary of State of Puerto Rico and 2nd Secretary of Public Safety of Puerto Rico</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Albino" title="Johnny Albino">Johnny Albino</a> (1919\xe2\x80\x932011) \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Bolero" title="Bolero">bolero</a> vocalist</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benny_Ayala" title="Benny Ayala">Benny Ayala</a> (born 1951) \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Series" title="1983 World Series">1983 World Series</a>-winning left fielder for the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carmelo_Filardi" title="Carmelo Filardi">Carmelo Filardi</a> - cartoonist who published El Mundo in 1927</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Fraticelli" title="Harry Fraticelli">Harry Fraticelli</a> (born 1944) - singer and musician</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mihiel_Gilormini" title="Mihiel Gilormini">Mihiel Gilormini</a> (1918\xe2\x80\x931988) \xe2\x80\x93 airman of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Founded the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Air_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico Air National Guard">Puerto Rico Air National Guard</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Lluch_Mora" title="Francisco Lluch Mora">Francisco Lluch Mora</a> (1924\xe2\x80\x932006) \xe2\x80\x93 poet and history professor</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Mattei_Lluberas" title="Antonio Mattei Lluberas">Antonio Mattei Lluberas</a> (1857\xe2\x80\x931908) \xe2\x80\x93 leader of the <a href="/wiki/Intentona_de_Yauco" title="Intentona de Yauco">Intentona de Yauco</a> against Spanish rule</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Andr%C3%A9s_Negroni" title="H\xc3\xa9ctor Andr\xc3\xa9s Negroni">H\xc3\xa9ctor Andr\xc3\xa9s Negroni</a> (born 1938) \xe2\x80\x93 first Puerto Rican graduate of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mike_P%C3%A9rez_(baseball)" title="Mike P\xc3\xa9rez (baseball)">Mike Perez</a> (born 1964) \xe2\x80\x93 1990s <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> pitcher</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Rojas_Tollinchi" title="Francisco Rojas Tollinchi">Francisco Rojas Tollinchi</a> (1911\xe2\x80\x931965) \xe2\x80\x93 poet and journalist.<sup id="cite_ref-JDLOFRT_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JDLOFRT-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Semidei_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Semidei Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Jos\xc3\xa9 Semidei Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> (1868\xe2\x80\x931958) \xe2\x80\x93 soldier in the Cuban Liberation Army in the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">Cuban War of Independence</a>, later Cuban diplomat.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ray_Suarez_(politician)" title="Ray Suarez (politician)">Ray Suarez</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Alderman" title="Alderman">alderman</a> in the 31st ward of <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a> since 1991</li></ul>\n<div
